It was first proposed by Francis Crick in 1958 and has since become a fundamental principle of molecular biology.\nThe process of gene expression involves several steps:\n1. Transcription: The first step in gene expression is transcription, where the information in a gene is copied from DNA to RNA. This process is carried out by enzymes called RNA polymerases, which read the DNA sequence and synthesize a complementary RNA molecule.\n2. RNA Processing: The RNA molecule produced by transcription is not yet ready to be translated into protein. It must undergo several processing steps, including splicing, capping, and polyadenylation, to produce a mature mRNA molecule.\n3. Translation: The mature mRNA molecule is then translated into protein by the ribosome, a complex of proteins and RNA molecules. The ribosome reads the mRNA sequence and assembles the amino acids into a protein according to the genetic code.\n4. Post-Translational Modifications: After translation, the protein may undergo further modifications, such as folding, glycosylation, or phosphorylation, to achieve its final structure and function.\nThe central dogma of molecular biology is a simplified model of gene expression, and it does not account for all the complexities of the process.
